Night
</a>




















</div>

<div
class="right_col
col-a-2">













<div
class="header
artist_info_header
int-1
clearfix">














<h1
class="hed-1"
title="Buffalo
Springfield"
itemprop="name">Buffalo
Springfield</h1>














<div
class="header_btns">















<div
class="bookmark"
data-musicid="R1844"></div>














</div>













</div>













<div
class="int-1">














<div
class="content_right">















<div
class="artist_bio_container
clearfix">
















<div
class="artist_bio
short_bio">
















<div
class="artist_bio_inner">

















Apart
from
the


















<a
href="/byrds"
class="hash">Byrds</a>,
no
other
American
band
had
as
great
an
impact
on
folk-rock
and
country-rock
--
really,
the
entire
Californian
rock
sound
--
than
Buffalo
Springfield.
The
group's
formation
is
the
stuff
of
legend:
driving
on
Sunset
Boulevard
in
Los
Angeles,


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stephen
Stills</a>
and


















<a
href="/richie-furay"
class="hash">Richie
Furay</a>
spotted
a
hearse
that


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>
was
sure
belonged
to


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Neil
Young</a>,
a
Canadian
he
had
crossed
paths
with
earlier.
Indeed
it
was,
and
with
the
addition
of
fellow
hearse
passenger
and
Canadian


















<a
href="/bruce-palmer"
class="hash">Bruce
Palmer</a>
on
bass
and
ex-

















<a
href="/dillards-artist"
class="hash">Dillard</a>
Dewey
Martin
on
drums,
the
cluster
of
ex-folkys
determined,
as


















<a
href="/byrds"
class="hash">the
Byrds</a>
had
just
done,
to
become
a
rock
&amp;
roll
band.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Buffalo
Springfield
wasn't
together
long
--
they
were
an
active
outfit
for
just
over
two
years,
between
1967
and
1968
--but
every
one
of
their
three
albums
was
noteworthy.
Their
debut,


















<a
href="#"
class="hash">Buffalo
Springfield</a>,
including
their
sole
big
hit
(

















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>'
&quot;For
What
It's
Worth&quot;),
established
them
as
the
best
folk-rock
band
in
the
land
barring


















<a
href="/byrds"
class="hash">the
Byrds</a>,
though
Springfield
was
a
bit
more
folk
and
country
oriented.


















<a
href="/buffalo-springfield/buffalo-springfield-again"
class="hash">Again</a>,
their
second
album
found
the
group
expanding
their
folk-rock
base
into
tough
hard
rock
and
psychedelic
orchestration,
resulting
in
their
best
record.
The
group
was
blessed
with
three
idiosyncratic,
talented
songwriters
in


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>,


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Young</a>,
and


















<a
href="/richie-furay"
class="hash">Furay</a>
(the
last
of
whom
didn't
begin
writing
until
the
second
LP)
yet
they
also
had
strong
and
often
conflicting
egos,
particularly


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>
and


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Young</a>.
The
group,
who
held
almost
infinite
promise,
rearranged
their
lineup
several
times,


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Young</a>
leaving
the
group
for
periods
and


















<a
href="/bruce-palmer"
class="hash">Palmer</a>
fighting
deportation,
until
disbanding
in
1968.
Their
final
album
clearly
shows
the
group
fragmenting
into
solo
directions.


















<br
/>

















<br
/>
Eventually,
the
inter-personal
tensions
and
creative
battles
led
to
a
perhaps
inevitable
split,
starting
with
Young's
departure
for
a
solo
career.
He
would
later
reunite
with


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stephen
Stills</a>
in


















<a
href="/crosby-stills-nash-young"
class="hash">Crosby,
Stills,
&amp;
Nash</a>,
joining
the
trio
once
a
decade
for
various
projects.
In
addition
to
CSN,


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>
released
solo
albums
and
worked
with
a
nother
band,
Manassas.
Initially,


















<a
href="/jim-messina"
class="hash">Jim
Messina</a>
and


















<a
href="/richie-furay"
class="hash">Richie
Furay</a>
stayed
together,
forming
the
country-rock
group


















<a
href="/poco"
class="hash">Poco</a>,
but


















<a
href="/jim-messina"
class="hash">Messina</a>
left
after
three
albums
to
team
up
in
a
duo
with


















<a
href="/kenny-loggins"
class="hash">Kenny
Loggins</a>.


















<a
href="/richie-furay"
class="hash">Furay</a>
himself
left


















<a
href="/poco"
class="hash">Poco</a>
and
teamed
with


















<a
href="/chris-hillman"
class="hash">Chris
Hillman</a>
and


















<a
href="/jd-souther"
class="hash">JD
Souther</a>
in
the
Souther
Hillman
Furay
Band
before
pursuing
a
solo
career.
Rumors
of
a
Buffalo
Springfield
reunion
circulated
for
years
--


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Young</a>
even
hinted
at
it
with
the
song
&quot;Buffalo
Springfield
Again&quot;
--and
it
finally
happened
in
the
fall
of
2010.


















<a
href="/neil-young"
class="hash">Young</a>,


















<a
href="/richie-furay"
class="hash">Furay</a>
and


















<a
href="/mike-bloomfield-al-kooper-steve-stills"
class="hash">Stills</a>
reunited
as
Buffalo
Springfield
for
a
pair
of
shows
at
Young's
annual
Bridge
School
Benefit
in
the
fall
of
2010.
It
wasn't
a
complete
reunion,
since


















<a
href="/bruce-palmer"
class="hash">Palmer</a>
had
died
in
2004
and
Martin
passed
in
2009,
but
the
three
singers
used
bassist
Rick
Rosas
and
drummer
Joe
Vitale
to
fill
in.
The
same
configuration
played
six
concerts
in
the
spring
of
2011,
but
reportedly
did
no
studio
work.
~
Richie
Unterberger
&amp;
Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine,
Rovi
















</div>















</div>
















<a
href="#"
class="full_bio_link">full
bio</a>















</div>

<script

Subscription

One
Gift

Terms
apply
to

One

(\"Purchaser\")

One

Subscription
online
or
by
purchasing
a
Pandora
One
Gift
Card
and
transferring

(\"Recipient\").
The

in

Pandora
is

		<li>To

Subscription

must
provide
valid
registration
information,
a
valid

and

at

time

purchase.

purchasing
a
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription,
you
authorize
Pandora
to
charge
the
purchase
price
of
the
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription,
and
any
applicable
sales,
telecommunication,

to
the

that

provide.</li>
		<li>The
Purchaser
is
not
entitled
to
a

or
credit
for
any
reason,
including,
without

if
the
Recipient

to

the
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription,
except

by
law.

a
Pandora
One
Gift

Pandora
One
Gift

Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription
online

see

for

		<li>The
Purchaser
may
not
transfer
a
single
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription
to
more
than
one
recipient.
A
Pandora
One
Gift
Subscription
is
fully
transferable
by
the
Recipient
prior
to
activation
or

In

event

by

or

Pandora
One
Gift

		<li>Recipients
may

Pandora
One
Gift
Subscriptions
at
